*  The next issue of commentary ran letters to the editor, who had the thankless job of choosing a few from among the flood that actually used language that was safe for publication. [[01:19:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4786.9s)]
*  Some people congratulated Pothoratz for his courage to write the essay, others were predictably outraged. [[01:19:58](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4798.9s)]
*  One of the latter was the black author and Village Voice columnist Joe Wood, who wrote a blistering essay in response for a book several years later, [[01:20:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4806.9s)]
*  in which he accused Pothoratz of harboring repressed homoerotic feelings for black men, of envy of the black penis, of Jewish self-hatred, and many other defects of body and character, and of course of racism. [[01:20:18](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4818.9s)]
*  Pothoratz is barking from the shadows, gentle reader. Don't be afraid. Read the record and see for yourself. [[01:20:33](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4833.9s)]
*  Remember how much the writer envied Negro strength? Notice how he fails to mention the millennia of stigma between Jewish past glory and imminent redemption. [[01:20:42](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4842.9s)]
*  Notice how easily his lunatic description of black experience could be used to describe Jewish experience. [[01:20:53](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4853.9s)]
*  And then dare to follow my reasoning to its unattractive and obvious conclusion. [[01:21:00](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4860.9s)]
*  At bottom, a profound self-hatred menaces in Pothoratz's essay. Each time he reveals his weakness as whiteness, he is confessing how much he hates his weakness as Jewishness, gentle reader. [[01:21:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4866.9s)]
*  Throughout his essay, Pothoratz unwittingly gives readers a glimpse of the peculiar blend of desire, anxiety, and racism that informed the Jewish-American discourse during the Depression. [[01:21:21](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4881.9s)]
*  This collision of impulses is never better revealed than in the writer's discussion of his black playmate named Carl. [[01:21:34](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4894.9s)]
*  It is here that Pothoratz comes closest to describing how his boyhood world shaped his ideas about black people. [[01:21:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4901.9s)]
*  The scrape with Carl is perfectly typical of New York City, where ethnic clashes are routine. [[01:21:47](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4907.9s)]
*  But the incident also condenses nicely a worldview peculiar to immigrant Jews at the time, which can be boiled down to a question. [[01:21:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4914.9s)]
*  With goyim slamming you from above and blacks threatening from below, what is a person to do? [[01:22:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4923.9s)]
*  In choosing to open his essay with a spotty memory of a black boy whose most notable feature is his moral equivalence to goyim, Pothoratz dismisses the idea of a special black moral station. [[01:22:10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4930.9s)]
*  It is an understandable move. African-Americans' history of subjugation has bestowed a moral authority historically reserved for Jews by Jews in Christian Europe. [[01:22:23](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4943.9s)]
*  Since Jewish-Americans could basically be themselves without the kind of penalties they had suffered in Europe, a Jewish identity based on that oppression made no sense. [[01:22:34](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4954.9s)]
*  One way to deal with the resultant confusion was to hate the displacers, the blacks. End quote. [[01:22:44](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4964.9s)]
*  And we're talking about kids here, but the black adults who had made the move up from the south, they were like most immigrants in the sense that they tended to keep their heads down and avoid conflict and do their best to conform to their new environment. [[01:22:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4972.9s)]
*  Their new circumstances were far from perfect, but these people were used to Jim Crow, and so it didn't seem so bad. [[01:23:10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4990.9s)]
*  They all knew from firsthand experience down south that attracting negative attention from white people usually carried very serious consequences, and so they tried to avoid conflict with them. [[01:23:16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=4996.9s)]
*  Their kids were a different story. By the early 60s, that first batch of black kids born in the northern and western ghettos, they were all white. [[01:23:26](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5006.9s)]
*  Their kids were a different story. By the early 60s, that first batch of black kids born in the northern and western ghettos, Baldwin and Wright, the people Potthoratz is talking about, the guys in school he's talking about, those kids have come of age by the early 60s. [[01:23:37](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5017.9s)]
*  And they had grown up going to school with the kids of working class white ethnics like the Potthoratz's. So unlike their parents, they did not fear white people. [[01:23:56](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5036.9s)]
*  They understood, like Potthoratz said rather, that white people were more likely to be afraid of them. [[01:24:07](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5047.9s)]
*  Potthoratz relates another incident that happened after he made the mistake of answering a teacher's question after a black boy named Quentin had gotten it wrong. [[01:24:14](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5054.9s)]
*  I had seen Quentin's face, a very dark, very cruel, very oriental looking face, hardened, and there had been enough threat in his eyes to make me run all the way home for fear that he might catch me outside. [[01:24:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5064.9s)]
*  Now, standing idly in front of my own house, I see him approaching from the project accompanied by his little brother who's carrying a baseball bat and wearing a grin of malicious anticipation. [[01:24:39](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5079.9s)]
*  As in a nightmare, I'm trapped. The surroundings are secure and familiar, but terror is suddenly present and there's no one around to help. [[01:24:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5091.9s)]
*  I'm locked to the spot. I will not cry out or run away like a sissy. And I stand there, my heart wild, my throat clogged. [[01:25:00](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5100.9s)]
*  He walks up, hurls the familiar epithet, hey mofucka, and to my surprise only pushes me. [[01:25:09](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5109.9s)]
*  It was a violent push, but not a punch. A push is not as serious as a punch. Maybe I can still back out without entirely losing my dignity. [[01:25:17](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5117.9s)]
*  Maybe I can still say, hey, come on, Quentin, what do you want to do that for? I didn't do nothing to you and walk away, but not too rapidly. [[01:25:27](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5127.9s)]
*  Instead, before I can stop myself, I push him back, a token gesture, and I say, cut that out. I don't want to fight. I ain't got nothing to fight about. [[01:25:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5136.9s)]
*  As I turn to walk back into the building, the corner of my eye catches the motion of the bat his little brother has handed to him. [[01:25:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5146.9s)]
*  I try to duck, but the bat crashes colored lights into my head. [[01:25:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5154.9s)]
*  The next thing I know, my mother and sister are standing over me, both of them hysterical. [[01:25:59](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5159.9s)]
*  My sister, she who is later to join the progressive youth organizations, is shouting for the police and screaming imprecations at those dirty little black bastards. [[01:26:05](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5165.9s)]
*  They take me upstairs, the doctor comes, the police come. I tell them that the boy who did it was a stranger, that he had been trying to get money from me. [[01:26:17](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5177.9s)]
*  They do not believe me, but I am too scared to give them Quentin's name. [[01:26:27](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5187.9s)]
*  When I return to school a few days later, Quentin avoids my eyes. He knows that I have not squealed, and he is ashamed. [[01:26:30](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5190.9s)]
*  I try to feel proud, but in my heart I know that it was fear of what his friends might do to me that had kept me silent, and not the coat of the street. [[01:26:39](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5199.9s)]
*  Having grown up in many poor neighborhoods where white kids like me were a vanishingly small part of the student population, and where I learned not to take a beating too personally, [[01:26:47](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5207.9s)]
*  I sometimes wonder how scenes like this are taken by people who grew up in more stable environments. [[01:27:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5224.9s)]
*  An unprovoked baseball bat attack is a pretty traumatic experience for a 12-year-old who is not used to violence. [[01:27:10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5230.9s)]
*  People are saying right now that all 12-year-olds should not be used to violence, but I and probably Pot Horitz can tell you that there are situations, at least, when some familiarity with it comes in handy. [[01:27:17](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5237.9s)]
*  Now, Joe Wood, Pot Horitz's critic that I just quoted a minute ago, he's got a point when he says that some of these encounters that have so shaped Pot Horitz's outlook are just examples of typical schoolyard bullying that happened to have had a more lingering effect on Pot Horitz because of the racial and political connotations that they had for him then and in real later life. [[01:27:28](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5248.9s)]
*  Now, Wood's point is that if Pot Horitz had gone to school with only Jews and Italians, say, then the Italian bullies would have picked on him for being Jewish. [[01:27:48](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5268.9s)]
*  And if you went to an all-Jewish school, Jewish bullies would have picked on him for wearing glasses or being skinny or something. [[01:27:59](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5279.9s)]
*  And that's true, up to a point. [[01:28:05](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5285.9s)]
*  Like I said, I went to several inner-city mostly black schools and I got jumped more than once by gangs of black kids. [[01:28:07](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5287.9s)]
*  I had my stuff stolen one time by a kid who was threatening me with a knife. [[01:28:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5295.9s)]
*  But I went to a lot of white and African-American schools and I got jumped more than once by gangs of black kids. [[01:28:19](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5299.9s)]
*  I had my stuff stolen one time by a kid who was threatening me with a knife. [[01:28:26](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5306.9s)]
*  But I went to a lot of white and Latino and mixed schools too and schools with a lot of Cambodians and Vietnamese and Laotians and Hmong students. [[01:28:33](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5313.9s)]
*  And I saw that kids got bullied at all of those schools and that the black schools I went to, black bullies went after black kids more than they went after me. [[01:28:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5323.9s)]
*  And so in other words, those experiences didn't imbue me with any deep-seated emotional triggers when it came to race, the same way Potthoratz confesses that his experiences did for him. [[01:28:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5332.9s)]
*  And yet on the other hand, Potthoratz knows something about what he's talking about too. [[01:29:05](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5345.9s)]
*  Because the fact is, there were Italians and Jews in his classes and they weren't the ones bullying him. [[01:29:11](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5351.9s)]
*  And furthermore, he says, the Jews and the Italians didn't really bully the black kids much, although the Italians did it more than the Jews. [[01:29:18](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5358.9s)]
*  Now this was still, at the time Potthoratz and Baldwin and Ryderall talking about when they were kids, this is still a relatively small issue. [[01:29:27](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5367.9s)]
*  One that did not touch the vast majority of New Yorkers. [[01:29:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5376.9s)]
*  Well that would change after World War II. [[01:29:40](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5380.9s)]
*  When World War II ended in 1945, there were about 130,000 black New Yorkers. [[01:29:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5383.9s)]
*  And by 1964, less than 20 years later, there were over 1.1 million African Americans in the city. [[01:29:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5392.9s)]
*  Just a massive, massive influx. [[01:30:01](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5401.9s)]
*  And I don't care who you are, I don't care who the natives in the city are or who the migrants to the city are. [[01:30:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5406.9s)]
*  There are going to be problems when you move nearly a million people into a city in less than 20 years. [[01:30:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5413.9s)]
*  And those problems are going to be even worse if the people moving in are not prepared for life in the city. [[01:30:20](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5420.9s)]
*  Many of the black migrants coming in, most of them, were impoverished, poorly educated by southern schools, [[01:30:28](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5428.9s)]
*  functionally illiterate country people with no real skills that were useful for an urban trade. [[01:30:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5435.9s)]
*  And that's not a dig on them. These people were mostly sharecroppers or small farmers down south. [[01:30:40](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5440.9s)]
*  Their segregated schools were less than ideal. [[01:30:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5446.9s)]
*  The same was true of the Irish migrants in the 19th century, by the way, and Italian immigrants later on. [[01:30:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5451.9s)]
*  Both of those groups were made up primarily of poor, unskilled, illiterate farmers from the hinterlands of their old countries. [[01:30:57](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5457.9s)]
*  And it was a huge and not always smooth adjustment to turn those folks into people who were fit for urban living. [[01:31:05](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5465.9s)]
*  The black migrants faced a major challenge that the previous migrants had not. [[01:31:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5475.9s)]
*  When the Irish and the Jews and the Italians showed up, and there were other immigrants to New York, obviously, [[01:31:22](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5482.9s)]
*  but those were the overwhelming majority of them, so those are the ones I'll talk mostly about. [[01:31:29](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5489.9s)]
*  When those three earlier groups showed up, New York City was still not really built out and populated. [[01:31:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5495.9s)]
*  At the peak of the Irish migration, a huge migration that totally transformed the city, [[01:31:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5501.9s)]
*  but at the peak of it, almost all New Yorkers still lived in a little strip of lower Manhattan, south of what's today Grand Street. [[01:31:48](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5508.9s)]
*  Most of the rest of Manhattan, it was still farmland, and the same was true in the outer boroughs. [[01:31:56](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5516.9s)]
*  By the time the Jews and Italians started showing up, things had been built up a lot, but there was still a lot of room. [[01:32:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5524.9s)]
*  And so when they showed up, they didn't have to push their way into established Irish Catholic parish communities. [[01:32:12](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5532.9s)]
*  They were able to spread out, and pretty soon there was a setup where everyone was basically comfortable with the new life. [[01:32:19](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5539.9s)]
*  Everyone was comfortable with the Irish living over there, the Jews over there, the Italians over there, [[01:32:26](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5546.9s)]
*  and where those neighborhoods bordered each other, the population would be mixed. [[01:32:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5551.9s)]
*  That was New York City. That was most big cities by the early 20th century. [[01:32:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5555.9s)]
*  But when black people started showing up in huge numbers after World War II, that situation had changed. [[01:32:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5561.9s)]
*  The city was more or less built and populated. [[01:32:49](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5569.9s)]
*  There would still be a lot of development, obviously. The Manhattan skyline would change a lot, [[01:32:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5572.9s)]
*  and there were some areas that hadn't been built up that would be later. [[01:32:58](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5578.9s)]
*  But in general, there was not a ton of room for newcomers, especially 900,000 newcomers in less than two decades. [[01:33:02](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5582.9s)]
*  There just wasn't a lot of room for them to take up in, and as a result, they did have to push in on established Irish, Jewish, and Italian neighborhoods [[01:33:11](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5591.9s)]
*  if they were going to find any place to live. [[01:33:20](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5600.9s)]
*  Now, the cities all tried to alleviate the situation. [[01:33:25](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5605.9s)]
*  Big public housing projects went up all over the country to house so many new people. [[01:33:28](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5608.9s)]
*  New social welfare programs and jobs programs were established. More schools and facilities were built. [[01:33:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5615.9s)]
*  But there was just no way that the cities were going to keep up with the pace of the migration, [[01:33:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5623.9s)]
*  and very quickly, the existing neighborhoods became extremely overcrowded, unpleasant places to live. [[01:33:47](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5627.9s)]
*  There wasn't enough housing, and the overcrowded housing that did exist started to deteriorate rapidly from so much population pressure. [[01:33:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5634.9s)]
*  By the 1960s, some black neighborhoods in Harlem were so overcrowded that, and this is from journalist Eugene Methven, [[01:34:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5643.9s)]
*  if the same density prevailed throughout New York City, the entire population of the United States in the 1960s could be jammed into just three of its five boroughs. [[01:34:14](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5654.9s)]
*  That is some serious population density. [[01:34:26](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5666.9s)]
*  City services could not meet the needs of so many people. The infrastructure couldn't support them. [[01:34:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5671.9s)]
*  The economy couldn't employ them, and the schools could not effectively educate all their kids. [[01:34:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5676.9s)]
*  The other main groups, the Italians, the Irish, and the Jews, they mostly got what they needed from the city because they were politically organized. [[01:34:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5683.9s)]
*  They elected politicians to local government from their own neighborhoods to go in and see to their needs, [[01:34:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5694.9s)]
*  and there would be political consequences if their needs were not met. [[01:35:01](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5701.9s)]
*  The black people in the city did not have anything like that yet. They weren't organized politically, [[01:35:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5706.9s)]
*  and so in a city that had been governed by ethnic politics for at least a century, [[01:35:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5713.9s)]
*  they were the one large demographic group with nobody working full-time to advocate for them, [[01:35:19](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5719.9s)]
*  which is another way of saying that as a neighborhood got blacker, it had less representation in city government, and so it was more neglected. [[01:35:26](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5726.9s)]
*  And this wasn't even really the result of racial discrimination, [[01:35:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5736.9s)]
*  so much as it was just a legacy of how the New York City political system had been structured over the years. [[01:35:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5741.9s)]
*  Ethnic politics, like I said, was taken for granted as a fact of life. [[01:35:47](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5747.9s)]
*  Nobody talked about identity politics the way they do today when Irish Catholics, to use an example, [[01:35:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5752.9s)]
*  voted for Irish Catholics from their neighborhood to go represent them. [[01:35:59](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5759.9s)]
*  It was just assumed that that was how things worked because, and this is something that really is different today to the point that it's hard for many of us to imagine, [[01:36:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5763.9s)]
*  it wasn't just that the city had X number of Irish people. [[01:36:12](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5772.9s)]
*  It had intact Irish Catholic parish communities that perceived themselves and were perceived by others as communities. [[01:36:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5775.9s)]
*  And I don't use that word community in the loose way that we use it today. [[01:36:23](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5783.9s)]
*  I mean that it was a well-organized corporate entity with networks and hierarchies and associations and political advocacy groups. [[01:36:28](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5788.9s)]
*  The community had a reality of its own. [[01:36:37](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5797.9s)]
*  It wasn't just a collection of individuals who happened to fit into the same category. [[01:36:39](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5799.9s)]
*  And so that's how things had always been. [[01:36:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5803.9s)]
*  But in the early days of the Great Migration, in the 30s and 40s and 50s, [[01:36:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5806.9s)]
*  the black population in New York had not developed that yet in any significant way. [[01:36:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5811.9s)]
*  And so as neighborhoods became blacker, they had less political influence. [[01:36:56](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5816.9s)]
*  And with less political influence, they were neglected and began to be neglected. [[01:37:01](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5821.9s)]
*  And as they began to decline, white people and eventually middle-class black people began to move out [[01:37:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5824.9s)]
*  and they took their social and economic capital with them. [[01:37:10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5830.9s)]
*  Over the course of just one or two decades, depending on the neighborhood, [[01:37:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5835.9s)]
*  neighborhoods that had been mostly white became mostly black. [[01:37:20](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5840.9s)]
*  Or in the case of New York City, black and middle-class people were mostly black. [[01:37:25](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5845.9s)]
*  The number of schools in New York City in which minorities, mostly black, [[01:37:28](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5848.9s)]
*  made up 90% or more of the student body tripled between 1955 and 1965. [[01:37:33](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5853.9s)]
*  Brownsville, the Brooklyn neighborhood where Podhoritz grew up, [[01:37:38](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5858.9s)]
*  it was still predominantly Jewish and Italian all the way up through the 1950s. [[01:37:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5863.9s)]
*  And so the black population was still very much in the middle-class. [[01:37:48](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5868.9s)]
*  And so the black population was still very much in the middle-class. [[01:37:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5872.9s)]
*  But by the late 1960s, it was still Jewish and Italian all the way up through the 1950s. [[01:37:55](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5875.9s)]
*  And by the late 60s, it was 95% black in Puerto Rican, 77% black, 18% Puerto Rican. [[01:38:00](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5880.9s)]
*  To put numbers on that, there was a Jewish community of about 175,000 in Brownsville [[01:38:08](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5888.9s)]
*  when Podhoritz was growing up, still well over 100,000 by 1955. [[01:38:16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5896.9s)]
*  But by the late 60s, there were only about 5,000 Jews left in Brownsville. [[01:38:20](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5900.9s)]
*  Other than the minority of beleaguered, mostly elderly Jews and Italians who remained behind, [[01:38:26](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5906.9s)]
*  the only white people with whom most of the black and brown majority ever interacted [[01:38:34](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5914.9s)]
*  were either representatives of authority, teachers, cops, social workers, [[01:38:40](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5920.9s)]
*  or representatives of capital, shopkeepers, landlords, pawnbrokers, and bosses. [[01:38:45](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5925.9s)]
*  So Brown versus the Board of Education, the Supreme Court decision desegregating southern schools, [[01:38:53](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5933.9s)]
*  kicked off the civil rights era in 1954. [[01:39:00](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5940.9s)]
*  A year after that, Rosa Parks, an employee and activist of the NAACP, [[01:39:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5944.9s)]
*  had her famous confrontation on a city bus in Montgomery, Alabama. [[01:39:10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5950.9s)]
*  She was arrested for refusing to give up her seat to a white person, [[01:39:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5955.9s)]
*  and Martin Luther King, Jr. rose to national prominence, [[01:39:20](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5960.9s)]
*  leading a year-long boycott of the Montgomery public transit system. [[01:39:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5964.9s)]
*  The civil rights movement had its golden age from about the time of that boycott, 1955-56, [[01:39:28](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5968.9s)]
*  up to about 1964. [[01:39:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5976.9s)]
*  In 1959, a series of sit-ins to desegregate facilities in Greensboro, North Carolina made headlines. [[01:39:38](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5978.9s)]
*  In 1961, the Freedom Riders, a group of black and white, mostly Jewish activists, [[01:39:47](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5987.9s)]
*  rode buses down into the deep south to force the issue after several states and cities refused to abide [[01:39:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=5994.9s)]
*  by the Supreme Court's ruling to desegregate. [[01:40:00](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6000.9s)]
*  In 1963, of course, was the March on Washington for Jobs and Freedom, [[01:40:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6003.9s)]
*  better known as the event where Martin Luther King gave his I Have a Dream speech. [[01:40:09](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6009.9s)]
*  And then in 1964 was the Mississippi Freedom Summer, [[01:40:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6013.9s)]
*  and it was here that cracks started to show up in the coalition. [[01:40:17](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6017.9s)]
*  Riding on the success of the March on Washington the year before, [[01:40:23](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6023.9s)]
*  black civil rights were the first to be recognized as a national organization. [[01:40:27](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6027.9s)]
*  In 1964, black civil rights organizations in Mississippi started recruiting volunteers [[01:40:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6031.9s)]
*  to spend the summer of 1964 on a massive effort to agitate, educate, [[01:40:37](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6037.9s)]
*  and organize black Mississippians for that year's elections. [[01:40:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6043.9s)]
*  White student organizations from northern universities wanted to help, and their help was wanted. [[01:40:48](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6048.9s)]
*  But the organizers requested no more than a hundred white volunteers from outside Mississippi [[01:40:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6054.9s)]
*  for reasons that would soon become apparent. [[01:40:59](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6059.9s)]
*  The Student Nonviolent Coordinating Committee, SNCC, [[01:41:05](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6065.9s)]
*  which was the largest southern-based black-led civil rights youth organization, [[01:41:09](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6069.9s)]
*  interviewed white volunteers to weed out ones with what they called a John Brown complex. [[01:41:16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6076.9s)]
*  The ones who made it through the screening process were warned that they were not there to save the Mississippi Negro. [[01:41:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6084.9s)]
*  They were there to assist the thousands of native black activists who had been on the ground [[01:41:32](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6092.9s)]
*  living and working for years before the white students arrived [[01:41:38](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6098.9s)]
*  and who would remain there long after the white kids went home for the fall semester. [[01:41:42](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6102.9s)]
*  But word got out that something big was brewing in Mississippi, [[01:41:48](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6108.9s)]
*  and that other student activists from around the country didn't want to miss out. [[01:41:53](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6113.9s)]
*  And so white civil rights activists like Allard Loewenstein started raising money [[01:41:57](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6117.9s)]
*  and recruiting more white students from universities outside the South. [[01:42:02](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6122.9s)]
*  And pretty soon, at least a thousand and probably several thousand over the course of the summer, [[01:42:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6126.9s)]
*  white students were flooding into the state to do their part. [[01:42:11](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6131.9s)]
*  Most of these student volunteers came from rich or at least upper-middle-class families [[01:42:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6135.9s)]
*  and were recruited from the top universities in the United States. [[01:42:20](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6140.9s)]
*  And they brought with them a variety of motives. [[01:42:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6144.9s)]
*  For sure, they were moved by sympathy for southern blacks. No question about it. [[01:42:28](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6148.9s)]
*  But a lot of them also pictured the freedom summer as their own personal hero quest. [[01:42:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6155.9s)]
*  Back at Columbia and Cornell and NYU and Harvard, [[01:42:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6161.9s)]
*  the activists who had gone south to work as volunteers or citizen journalists in the previous summers, [[01:42:45](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6165.9s)]
*  they were the aristocracy of the student movement. [[01:42:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6172.9s)]
*  And a lot of students saw Mississippi as their one way to get to cool kid status back on campus. [[01:42:55](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6175.9s)]
*  That meant they had different goals and were working on a different timeline than the local blacks. [[01:43:01](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6181.9s)]
*  Because whereas the blacks had been and would be working for years at the grassroots level in the state, [[01:43:08](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6188.9s)]
*  the white students only had a few months to make something happen that would give them some good stories to tell [[01:43:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6193.9s)]
*  and make their trip worthwhile before they had to head back to school. [[01:43:19](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6199.9s)]
*  Now, it seems I'm being a little bit ungenerous to the white activists. [[01:43:23](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6203.9s)]
*  Maybe I am, but I am only repeating the complaints that would become common among many of the native black activists by the end of the summer. [[01:43:30](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6210.9s)]
*  The sympathy of the college kids for the people they were trying to help, it was real. [[01:43:40](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6220.9s)]
*  I don't want to sound like I'm denying that. [[01:43:45](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6225.9s)]
*  But it was also a sympathy that was distant and detached and could come across as condescending and patronizing. [[01:43:48](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6228.9s)]
*  When the rubber hit the road and a group of Harvard Law students found themselves in a room full of black Mississippians with an elementary school education, [[01:43:55](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6235.9s)]
*  their eagerness, a less generous person would say their impatience to move things along, [[01:44:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6244.9s)]
*  often led to them just taking over the proceedings and effectively ordering the black activists around. [[01:44:12](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6252.9s)]
*  You can kind of understand how that could happen. [[01:44:18](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6258.9s)]
*  Even if the person has nothing but good, pure intentions, [[01:44:21](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6261.9s)]
*  if you are a group of students from Harvard Law with lots of experience in political organizing with SDS or some other campus group, [[01:44:25](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6265.9s)]
*  you probably do know better than other people how to best get things done. [[01:44:32](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6272.9s)]
*  But you can't just come into someone's home and start ordering them around no matter what your intentions are. [[01:44:38](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6278.9s)]
*  And so over the summer months, resentment and enthusiasm grew side by side. [[01:44:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6283.9s)]
*  And when the freedom summer failed to achieve any immediate political results in the 64 elections, [[01:44:50](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6290.9s)]
*  which is not to say it wasn't a success in other ways, [[01:44:57](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6297.9s)]
*  it opened up the door to a new breed of black leaders like Stokely Carmichael, [[01:44:59](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6299.9s)]
*  who started putting out the message that they were never going to get anywhere following the lead of bossy white students and philanthropists. [[01:45:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6306.9s)]
*  Carmichael had grown up in New York. [[01:45:14](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6314.9s)]
*  And so while southern black activists were following the lead of Martin Luther King and the other black ministers of the SCLC, [[01:45:17](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6317.9s)]
*  Carmichael had been steeped in the rhetoric of Malcolm X and other black militants in Harlem. [[01:45:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6324.9s)]
*  And he brought that attitude to the southern movement, probably more forcefully than anyone else, especially once he became the chairman of SNCC. [[01:45:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6331.9s)]
*  What Carmichael was saying, it really didn't make a lot of sense at face value, you know, [[01:45:40](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6340.9s)]
*  given that all of the civil rights movements' major successes, the desegregation decisions at the Supreme Court, [[01:45:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6346.9s)]
*  the Civil Rights Act of 64, the Voting Rights Act of 65, all of them, they were all achieved by the very people Carmichael [[01:45:55](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6355.9s)]
*  and people like him were calling Uncle Toms and their white allies. [[01:46:02](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6362.9s)]
*  But still, the experience of many black people with the white activists that summer [[01:46:07](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6367.9s)]
*  opened up space for them to think maybe Carmichael had a point and that maybe the movement's emphasis on reconciliation [[01:46:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6373.9s)]
*  and incremental improvement in nonviolence, maybe that reflected the existing leadership's excessive deference to white society. [[01:46:21](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6381.9s)]
*  And so SNCC and other youth organizations emerged from the freedom summer with a new edginess, [[01:46:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6391.9s)]
*  although it would be a few years before people look back and realize that it probably represented the high water mark of the civil rights movement. [[01:46:37](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6397.9s)]
*  A couple years later, under Carmichael's leadership, SNCC would purge all of its white members. [[01:46:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6406.9s)]
*  And then he turned the organization over to a young criminal named H. Rapp Brown to lead SNCC through the worst of the riot years. [[01:46:53](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6413.9s)]
*  In 1965, despite the Selma March and the passage of the Voting Rights Act, the golden years of the civil rights movement came to an end. [[01:47:00](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6420.9s)]
*  Partly that was because everything that could be achieved from a legal standpoint had pretty much been achieved. [[01:47:12](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6432.9s)]
*  And the southern civil rights leaders who had spent so many years fighting for straightforward demands of legal equality [[01:47:21](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6441.9s)]
*  weren't exactly sure where to go from there, and so they started to lose influence. [[01:47:29](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6449.9s)]
*  It was becoming obvious by then that the problems of the northern ghettos were by far the most pressing issue for black people in America. [[01:47:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6455.9s)]
*  Things were starting to get really bad in a lot of inner cities, but the reasons were much more complicated than down south. [[01:47:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6466.9s)]
*  The cities were segregated, as segregated as anywhere in the south, but not by law. [[01:47:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6474.9s)]
*  And black people faced discrimination, but not officially. It was interpersonal. [[01:48:01](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6481.9s)]
*  The people who were still down south, yes, there was segregation, there was discrimination, there was government neglect, [[01:48:09](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6489.9s)]
*  but at least black southerners were still living in mostly intact families with communities that could engage in a certain amount of collective self-help and gave people a social context to live in. [[01:48:18](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6498.9s)]
*  In the north, the whole fabric of black community life had been torn apart by the pressures brought to bear on people by the Great Migration. [[01:48:32](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6512.9s)]
*  That year, 1965, the Irish American scholar and future New York Senator, Daniel Patrick Moynihan, was working for the Labor Department, and he authored a report on the ongoing collapse of the black family. [[01:48:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6521.9s)]
*  And he pointed out that his Irish immigrant ancestors had had a similar experience when they'd arrived in America. [[01:48:57](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6537.9s)]
*  He wrote, [[01:49:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6544.9s)]
*  It was this abrupt transition that produced the wild Irish slums of the 19th century northeast. Drunkenness, crime, corruption, discrimination, family disorganization, juvenile delinquency were the routine of that era. [[01:49:34](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6574.9s)]
*  In our own time, the same sudden transition has produced the Negro slum, different from, but hardly better than its predecessors, and fundamentally the result of the same process. [[01:49:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6591.9s)]
*  In 1939, African American sociologist E. Franklin Frazier described its plight movingly in that part of The Negro Family entitled In the City of Destruction. [[01:50:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6603.9s)]
*  Now quoting Frazier, [[01:50:14](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6614.9s)]
*  The impact of hundreds of thousands of rural southern Negroes upon northern metropolitan communities presents a bewildering spectacle. [[01:50:16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6616.9s)]
*  Striking contrasts in levels of civilization and economic well-being among these newcomers to modern civilization seem to baffle any attempt to discover order and direction in their mode of life. End quote. [[01:50:25](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6625.9s)]
*  Now it wasn't that all black Americans were on a one-way slide downhill as they moved into the cities. Not at all. [[01:50:39](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6639.9s)]
*  What was really happening was the black population of America was splitting up and heading in opposite directions. [[01:50:49](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6649.9s)]
*  The black middle class was growing throughout this period. [[01:50:57](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6657.9s)]
*  Incomes had risen 150% between 1940 and 1960. [[01:51:01](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6661.9s)]
*  Black homeownership had gone from 23% to 38% in that same period. [[01:51:07](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6667.9s)]
*  Between 1940 and 1970, the percentage of black men holding down white-colored jobs increased more than 400%. [[01:51:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6673.9s)]
*  And black life expectancy improved from 53 years in 1940 to 63.6 years in 1960. [[01:51:23](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6683.9s)]
*  Now under normal circumstances, these numbers could only be seen as evidence of astounding success, helping an underprivileged group catch up with the rest of society. [[01:51:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6691.9s)]
*  But the problem was that the improvements were only being felt by a part of the black population. [[01:51:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6703.9s)]
*  And in the meantime, a whole lot of people, the ones who were not part of the increase in homeownership or white-colored jobs, were watching their situation rapidly getting much worse. [[01:51:49](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6709.9s)]
*  In his book, The Culture of Narcissism, the American social critic Christopher Lash complained that in the 60s and 70s, left-wing politics in America became less about getting anything done to actually help the lives of people at the bottom, and much more about their self-esteem and identity and authenticity. [[01:52:02](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6722.9s)]
*  Less a vehicle for collective change, in other words, than for individual self-expression. [[01:52:29](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6749.9s)]
*  Another social critic, Eric Hoffer, wrote about the effects on people of going through periods of intense and unpredictable change. [[01:52:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6756.9s)]
*  He wrote that, [[01:52:45](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6765.9s)]
*  And it is also a reaction against loss of balance, a swinging and flailing of the arms to regain one's balance and keep afloat. [[01:53:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6795.9s)]
*  Thus, drastic change is one of the agencies which release man's energies. [[01:53:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6804.9s)]
*  But certain conditions have to be present if the shock of change is to turn people into effective men of action. [[01:53:29](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6809.9s)]
*  There must be an abundance of opportunities. [[01:53:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6816.9s)]
*  There must be a tradition of self-reliance. [[01:53:39](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6819.9s)]
*  Given these conditions, a population subjected to drastic change will plunge into an orgy of action. [[01:53:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6821.9s)]
*  The millions of immigrants dumped on our shores after the Civil War underwent a tremendous change, and it was a highly irritating and painful experience. [[01:53:49](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6829.9s)]
*  Not only were they transferred, almost overnight, to a wholly foreign world, but they were, for the most part, torn from the warm communal existence of a small town or village somewhere in Europe, and exposed to the cold and dismal isolation of individual existence. [[01:53:58](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6838.9s)]
*  They were misfits in every sense of the word, and ideal material for a revolutionary explosion. [[01:54:16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6856.9s)]
*  But they had a vast continent at their disposal, and fabulous opportunities for self-advancement, and an environment which held self-reliance and individual enterprise in high esteem. [[01:54:23](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6863.9s)]
*  And so these immigrants from stagnant small towns and villages in Europe plunged into a mad pursuit of action. [[01:54:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6875.9s)]
*  They tamed and mastered a continent in an incredibly short time, and we are still in the backwash of that mad pursuit. [[01:54:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6883.9s)]
*  But then he says, [[01:54:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6891.9s)]
*  Things are different when people subjected to drastic change find only meager opportunities for action, or when they cannot, or are not allowed to, attain self-confidence and self-esteem by individual pursuits. [[01:54:53](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6893.9s)]
*  When a population undergoing drastic change is without abundant opportunities for individual action and self-advancement, it develops a hunger for faith, pride, and unity. [[01:55:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6904.9s)]
*  It becomes receptive to all manner of proselytizing, and is eager to throw itself into collective undertakings which aim at showing the world. [[01:55:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6915.9s)]
*  In other words, drastic change, under certain conditions, creates a proclivity for fanatical attitudes, united action, and spectacular manifestations of flouting and defiance. [[01:55:25](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6925.9s)]
*  It creates, in short, an atmosphere of revolution. [[01:55:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6936.9s)]
*  We are usually told that revolutions are set in motion to realize radical changes. [[01:55:40](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6940.9s)]
*  Actually, it is drastic change which sets the stage for revolution. [[01:55:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6946.9s)]
*  The revolutionary mood and temper are generated by the irritations, difficulties, hungers, and frustrations inherent in the environment. [[01:55:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6951.9s)]
*  The revolutionary mood and temper are generated by the irritations, difficulties, hungers, and frustrations inherent in the realization of drastic change. [[01:55:58](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6958.9s)]
*  Where things have not changed at all, there is the least likelihood of revolution. [[01:56:08](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6968.9s)]
*  Well, that passage right there explains pretty clearly why riotous militancy and extremist separatism among African Americans got going up in the North, among the people undergoing the drastic changes of the Great Migration, [[01:56:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6973.9s)]
*  and who had been yanked out of a southern milieu where they were poor and discriminated against, but where they had some continuity with the past, and some community, and more or less intact families. [[01:56:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=6991.9s)]
*  And they were thrust into an environment up North where everybody felt alone in their dingy run-down tenement or housing project in Detroit or Chicago, New York. [[01:56:43](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7003.9s)]
*  And as Hoffer writes, quote, The result was not emancipation, but isolation and exposure. [[01:56:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7014.9s)]
*  An immature individual was torn from the warmth and security of a corporate existence and left orphaned and empty in a cold world. [[01:57:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7023.9s)]
*  It has been often said that power corrupts, but it is perhaps equally important to realize that weakness, too, corrupts. [[01:57:13](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7033.9s)]
*  Power corrupts the few, while weakness corrupts the many. Hatred, malice, rudeness, intolerance, and suspicion are the fruits of weakness. End quote. [[01:57:22](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7042.9s)]
*  Now, Hoffer wrote that book in 1963, and he had more in mind the post-colonial revolutions in the Third World when he talked about drastic change leading to turmoil. [[01:57:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7055.9s)]
*  But two years after he published it, in 1965, it became clear to everyone that he did not have to look that far from home to prove his thesis. [[01:57:47](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7067.9s)]
*  And when people think of the most important years of the Civil Rights era, people might point to 1954, the Brown versus Board of Education decision, maybe 1963 when Martin Luther King gave his famous speech, or 1968 when King was killed. [[01:57:58](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7078.9s)]
*  But I think 1965 was the most important turning point. [[01:58:18](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7098.9s)]
*  That year, Martin Luther King led the march to Selma, Alabama, and the Voting Rights Act was signed into law. And that's what most people remember about 1965 when it comes to civil rights. [[01:58:23](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7103.9s)]
*  But it was also the year Malcolm X was murdered, and it was the year of the Watts riots in Los Angeles. [[01:58:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7116.9s)]
*  The Watts riots changed the way the whole country looked at the race question. [[01:58:44](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7124.9s)]
*  It all started over the police trying to arrest a drunk driver and then getting into a scuffle with some of the neighborhood people who tried to interfere. [[01:58:49](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7129.9s)]
*  But as with most race riots, the proximate cause was really not that important. [[01:58:57](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7137.9s)]
*  Something like Watts does not happen because some drunk gets roughhoused by the cops. [[01:59:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7143.9s)]
*  Something like that builds for a long time. [[01:59:08](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7148.9s)]
*  Well, once it kicked off, reporters could not go into the riot zone without being attacked. [[01:59:10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7150.9s)]
*  But TV news helicopters kept a live broadcast up for five nights, and the nation sat in front of their TVs and witnessed destruction on a level that they had never really considered before, in peacetime at least. [[01:59:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7155.9s)]
*  Nobody alive had ever seen anything like it because nothing like it had really happened since the draft riots during the Civil War. [[01:59:27](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7167.9s)]
*  Aerial shots showed crowds of black people setting buildings on fire and then dancing around the flames. [[01:59:38](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7178.9s)]
*  And then the police came out and started shooting at the people who were there. [[01:59:45](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7185.9s)]
*  Aerial shots showed crowds of black people setting buildings on fire and then dancing around the flames and then attacking and chasing away firefighters who showed up to try to put out the flames. [[01:59:50](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7190.9s)]
*  Some rioters gave interviews and they were promising that the violence was soon going to spread into the suburbs and into the neighborhoods and homes of white people. [[02:00:03](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7203.9s)]
*  More than once, viewers saw the TV news helicopter providing their live feed have to flee the scene because it started taking small arms fire from the ground. [[02:00:12](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7212.9s)]
*  The scale and aggression of the violence in Watts was unprecedented in modern America at least. [[02:00:25](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7225.9s)]
*  The televised scene seemed to portray a mindlessness and nihilism that was unfamiliar to people for whom Rosa Parks and MLK had always been the face of the black struggle in America. [[02:00:35](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7235.9s)]
*  Historian Fred Siegel wrote, [[02:00:52](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7252.9s)]
*  Watts was unlike any earlier riot. We are still living in its aftermath. [[02:00:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7254.9s)]
*  Watts, the first major riot to be televised, inspired subsequent rebellions in Washington, D.C., Detroit, and Newark. [[02:01:00](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7260.9s)]
*  The immediate damage to Los Angeles was obvious. 34 people, almost all black, were dead. [[02:01:09](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7269.9s)]
*  Whole blocks had been razed and almost 4,000 people were killed. [[02:01:16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7276.9s)]
*  Much of Watts was never rebuilt and neither was the relative optimism regarding race and integration that had briefly held sway in the wake of the historic 1963 civil rights march on Washington. [[02:01:21](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7281.9s)]
*  The immediate response to Watts was to see it as the work of a small group of street tufts and criminals. [[02:01:31](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7291.9s)]
*  The tufts were involved, but the breadth of the participation in the march was not enough to see it as a result of the violence. [[02:01:39](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7299.9s)]
*  The tufts were involved, but the breadth of the participation suggested something much more ominous. [[02:01:48](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7308.9s)]
*  Los Angeles was a city with an expanding black middle class, a city that, according to a National Urban League survey, ranked first among major American cities in the quality of black life. [[02:01:55](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7315.9s)]
*  Yet post-riot surveys showed that the rioters represented a cross-section of black South Central Los Angeles. [[02:02:08](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7328.9s)]
*  What had happened for blacks of all classes was that the surge in collective consciousness flowing out of the Southern civil rights struggle broke down barriers to the expression of the rage and hostility that had built up for so long. [[02:02:15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7335.9s)]
*  The primitive rebels of the Watts uprising, some of them gang members, were little concerned with integration and much concerned with authenticity and the power of violence to wipe away historic humiliations. [[02:02:30](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7350.9s)]
*  Paul Williams, a young participant in the riots, described their almost mystical effect on him. [[02:02:45](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7365.9s)]
*  Mass media coverage of the Watts riots caused the race riot to metastasize in the same way that nationwide coverage of the Columbine High School massacre led to the proliferation of school shootings. [[02:02:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7371.9s)]
*  Neither event was the first of its kind, but the coverage transformed them into something more than local atrocities and opened up a new set of possibilities in the fight against the [[02:03:04](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7384.9s)]
*  mass media. [[02:03:09](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7389.9s)]
*  The mass media coverage of the Watts riots caused the race riot to metastasize in the same way that nationwide coverage of the Columbine High School massacre led to the proliferation of school shootings. [[02:03:10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7390.9s)]
*  Neither event was the first of its kind, but the coverage transformed them into something more than local atrocities and opened up a new set of possibilities in the minds of many people across the country. [[02:03:22](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7402.9s)]
*  The writer and veteran of the 60s revolutions, Paul Berman, wrote that one of the remarkable things about the era was how rapidly new ideas migrated from fringe opinions to being consensus truths. [[02:03:37](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7417.9s)]
*  The Black Panthers, Mao and Malcolm inspired militant rhetoric was only heard from a few Harlem street preachers in the early 1960s. [[02:03:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7434.9s)]
*  But by the summer of 66, 67, it was the predominant rhetoric of inner city activists everywhere. [[02:04:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7446.9s)]
*  An ideology of rebellion, rejection and defiance for their own sake as goods in themselves had firmly taken hold. [[02:04:14](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7454.9s)]
*  Until 1965, the Students for a Democratic Society, SDS, which was the largest and most important left wing student group in the country. [[02:04:27](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7467.9s)]
*  Until 1965, it had just been the youth wing of the stodgy old Social Democratic League for Industrial Democracy. [[02:04:38](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7478.9s)]
*  By 1967, Maoist radicals and nascent terrorists were battling for control of the organization. [[02:04:46](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7486.9s)]
*  Berman writes that by the 67, 68 school year, quote, By holding daily demonstrations, by doing something outrageous or impudent against the war or American racism, [[02:04:55](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7495.9s)]
*  by disrupting an occasional class or heckling a professor, preferably a good liberal whose sin was to stand one inch to the right of the student left, [[02:05:07](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7507.9s)]
*  by dressing slightly differently from the other students, in short, by resisting much, obeying little, [[02:05:16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7516.9s)]
*  the movement generated an atmosphere of confrontation, which turned giddy and hot, which created a festival atmosphere, which got hotter. [[02:05:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7524.9s)]
*  There was a feeling that every aspect of the existing society had been discovered to be wrong and could be opposed. [[02:05:33](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7533.9s)]
*  That in the splendid carnival of the student demonstrations and rock concerts in hippie neighborhoods and the continual insurrections of individuals, [[02:05:41](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7541.9s)]
*  a revolution had already occurred. That the new society and newer ways of living already existed in embryo. [[02:05:51](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7551.9s)]
*  All you had to do was join. The marches, the building takeovers, the amphetamine activism that went on night and day, [[02:05:59](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7559.9s)]

*  and showing their willingness to always go further when others might pull back. That's how you got your face in a news story. [[02:06:44](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7604.9s)]
*  This was happening in both the white and black protest movements with the important difference that the two were working with very different human material. [[02:06:54](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7614.9s)]
*  The black kids were tougher and more daring than the white college kids who always had one eye on the degrees and the careers that they expected to follow their protest phase. [[02:07:06](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7626.9s)]
*  The movement was for them a means to accrue valuable experiences that would give them credibility among the people whose opinions they cared about and to give themselves a sense of meaning and authenticity in their lives. [[02:07:20](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7640.9s)]
*  The black kids were much more serious, much more angry, or at least they had better reasons to be. [[02:07:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7656.9s)]
*  The white kids were aware of the deficiency and did what they could to overcompensate for it. Kirkpatrick Sale, in his history of SDS, wrote about an incident at Columbia University involving a leader of the weatherman terrorist cell named Mark Rudd and a less radical, non-weatherman SDSer named Paul Rockwell. [[02:07:45](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7665.9s)]
*  Columbia at the time had been taken over by student radicals and many of them were armed and had taken over buildings and some were holding hostages while they made demands on the university. [[02:08:08](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7688.9s)]
*  And so at a rally, Rudd's up on stage trying to get everybody riled up. [[02:08:19](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7699.9s)]
*  quote, Rudd, in heavy boots, work shirt, leather jacket, and cloth cap, gave off vibrations of restless energy during his speech, pacing back and forth at audience level in front of an unused podium brandishing a chair leg, yelling at the students there for being soft and wimpy, and bragging of how he was preparing for the revolution. [[02:08:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7704.9s)]
*  I've got myself a gun. Has everyone here got a gun? Anyone? Well, you better fucking get your shit together. [[02:08:47](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7727.9s)]
*  After some 15 to 20 minutes of this, Paul Rockwell, a short, stocky SDSer, got out of his seat and moved toward the front of the room, declaring that Rudd had had his turn and now he wanted to speak. [[02:08:58](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7738.9s)]
*  Rudd took two menacing steps toward Rockwell, hulking over him, but Rockwell just barreled ahead, slammed Rudd into the podium, pushed Rudd's fists away, and turned to face the audience. [[02:09:11](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7751.9s)]
*  Rudd's face was a picture of stunned fear, all his rhetoric having done nothing to overcome his ingrained middle-class unfamiliarity with and anxiety about violence. [[02:09:24](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7764.9s)]
*  He stood there a moment, shrugged, then slunk off to join his friends to one side. The macho mood was dissipated, and no one seemed to have joined the weathermen ranks that night. [[02:09:36](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7776.9s)]
*  So white revolutionaries like Paul Rudd, rather Mark Rudd, Paul Rockwell, confusing. [[02:09:49](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7789.9s)]
*  White revolutionaries like Mark Rudd knew their limitations better than anybody, and so they all worshiped the black revolutionaries for their animal courage and their apparent lack of concern for consequences. [[02:09:59](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ga0tyBtGAds&t=7799.9s)]
